<span id="freeTextContainer1523359573527869787">Oh THIS BOOK. So, the truth of the matter is <b>I really really <i>absolutely seriously</i> love dragons.</b> So I'm already biased to love this book. AND I DO. I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17331828.Talon__Talon___1_' title='Talon (Talon, #1) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Talon</a> was better. (So if you loathed Talon, don't even try this one.) But I still loved the action, the attitudes, the sly wit, and the draaaaagons. DID I MENTION I LOVE DRAGONS?<br/><br/>I FREAKING LOVE DRAGONS.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438234544ra/15682446.gif' width='500' height='301' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Ahem.<br/><br/><b>So this book literally takes off where the last one ended.</b> Garett is about to be executed. Riley/Cobalt is being tough and grumpy (he prob</span>
  <span id="freeText1523359573527869787" style="display:none">Oh THIS BOOK. So, the truth of the matter is <b>I really really <i>absolutely seriously</i> love dragons.</b> So I'm already biased to love this book. AND I DO. I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17331828.Talon__Talon___1_" title="Talon (Talon, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Talon</a> was better. (So if you loathed Talon, don't even try this one.) But I still loved the action, the attitudes, the sly wit, and the draaaaagons. DID I MENTION I LOVE DRAGONS?<br><br>I FREAKING LOVE DRAGONS.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438234544ra/15682446.gif" width="500" height="301" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ahem.<br><br><b>So this book literally takes off where the last one ended.</b> Garett is about to be executed. Riley/Cobalt is being tough and grumpy (he probably needs a snack, tbh). Ember is flipping her hair and sassing. And Dante is getting swallowed by the Talon organisation and preened for a position of great power. We get 4 POVs, which isn't my <i>favourite</i>. AKA I really liked reading Embera nd Garrett and also Dante (there was so not enough Dante) BUT RILEY? I DO NOT CARE. <br><br>My feelings towards Riley are basically: Turn the moody fool into a scaly handbag.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/273228.gif" width="225" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Unfortunately the book is like 60% ABOUT Riley. We get a lot of his backstory, and a toooon of his POV (he's probably go the most chapters) and his moody brain made me want to stab him with a spork. Gah. <br><br>Also, because apparently book one wasn't okay with just a forbidden romance...**drumroll* <b>WELCOME TO THE LOVE TRIANGLE.</b> Riley, who is 20+ years old, is now crushing so passionately on Ember he MANIPULATES HER WITH HIS EMOTIONS. Dude, that is wrong. She feels to guilty because he loves her so so much...and she doesn't even like him. At least that's the vibe I get. And despite risking everything to bust Garrett out of prison...Ember's sitting there wondering if she likes Riley? WOMAN. YOU DO NOT. YOU LIKE GARRETT. DARN IT. And Garrett did absolutely nothing in this book, darn it, which made me sad. I liked him a lot in bk 1! He's having a lot of emotional conflicts, though, so that was interesting. There was just waaaaay too much Riley. ERK.<br><br><b>I also still have a LOT of questions about the world building.</b> Like apparently Talon wants to take over human kind and rule it. Like, I get that. It's a great goal (also, mine) but whyyyyy? Like what do they want to gain? What is going on in their brains? I WANT TO KNOW TALON'S MOTIVES. I feel like bk 2 should've fleshed this out more.<br><br>Also the middle dragged like a slug in peanut butter. That's sad.<br><br><b>BUT I LOVED THE WRITING AND I LOVE DRAGONS AND I QUITE LOVE THIS SERIES.</b> I love the military vibe and how exciting the action scenes are and. HELLO, they use <i>dragons</i> AND <i>guns</i>. That is awesome. So while the characters kind of belly-flopped in a dragon pizza for me (I don't even know what that means, but don't question my metaphors) I still LOVE the idea of super slick neat secret-agent-ish dragon organisations. <br><br>I LOVE THE COVERS TOO. <br><br>I WANNA BE A DRAGON.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438234544ra/15682447.gif" width="410" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>

<div id="review_1446091616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446091616" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446091616?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-roxanne">reviewed-by-roxanne</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446091616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9867345281088731213">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br/><br/>Quick & Dirty: Dragons, war, betrayal, and so much more….seriously epic tale of Ember, Dante, Garrett and Cobalt/Riley.<br/><br/>Opening Sentence: “I stood before a silent, watchful table, six pairs of eyes on me, keen gazes ranging from suspicious to appraising as we waited for the charges to be declared.”<br/><br/>The Review:<br/><br/>Ember, Garrett, Dante and Cobalt/Riley are back in book 2 shortly after the epicness of book one ends. From this point forth if you haven’t read Talon plea</span>
  <span id="freeText9867345281088731213" style="display:none">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br /><br />Quick &amp; Dirty: Dragons, war, betrayal, and so much more….seriously epic tale of Ember, Dante, Garrett and Cobalt/Riley.<br /><br />Opening Sentence: “I stood before a silent, watchful table, six pairs of eyes on me, keen gazes ranging from suspicious to appraising as we waited for the charges to be declared.”<br /><br />The Review:<br /><br />Ember, Garrett, Dante and Cobalt/Riley are back in book 2 shortly after the epicness of book one ends. From this point forth if you haven’t read Talon please stop and go read Talon because you won’t want to be spoiled. Ember convinces Riley to go in and they save Garrett before he is executed by the order. From there the three of them plus Wes go on the run, trying to outwit both the order and Talon. Meanwhile Dante is plotting and planning to recapture Ember and kill Riley.<br /><br />Ember, Garrett and Riley end up in Vegas trying to find ways to stay ahead of the order, when they hear rumors of a dragon sighting. They end up trying to rescue two hatchlings, and well you have to read the book…seriously! This book is action from the beginning until the very end. It’s fast paced and flies by.<br /><br />Julie Kagawa picks a subject and writes it in such a way that you just fall in love. I like dragons but have not liked a ton of dragon books, especially those with shifters. However, these aren’t shifter’s per se, they have a human form that they have learned over time to in order to blend in and hide from the Order of Saint George but these are most definitely dragons. This is a complex tale that she is weaving in which you really don’t have any idea who the good guys are, the dragons (Talon) are ruthlessly in control of the dragon world, forcing hatchlings into jobs and breeding them if they fail at those jobs. They also kill those who try to leave the fold or who really fail at their jobs. The humans (Order of Saint George) are just as ruthless in their pursuit of dragons, only drawing the line at waiting to see them in their true form before killing them. Riley/Cobalt is trained Basilisk that is trying to help and hide dragons from Talon.<br /><br />It’s a perfect storm of complexity that draws you in and you totally root for them to kick Talon and Order butt. My only real complaint is the love triangle. I am not a fan and usually she does a touch of it, but normally it’s pretty clear who the female lead is going to choose. In this one Ember is clearly torn between Garrett and Riley. I will say that there appears to be resolution at the end of this book, but given that Soldier is the name of the next book I am sure there will not be a real answer until the conclusion of book three. I love, love all of her books and Rogue was no different for me. I think this might have been the first time I didn’t cry at the ending of her second book, because let’s face it, she loves to rip your heart and leave you with a massive cliffhanger.<br /><br />So if dragons are your thing go get Talon and then Rogue! If they aren’t your thing go get them anyway because Julie will totally make them your thing when she is done with you! Seriously, I have read all of her books, and she is one of my go-to authors, I haven’t read a bad book by her.<br /><br />Notable Scenes:<br /><br />“The order wouldn’t stop hunting me, especially now that I was in the company of dragons.”<br /><br />“A talon operative had died in this building tonight.”<br /><br />“And Lilith’s voice, telling me I was born to become a Viper, a killer like her.”<br /><br />“The boy who didn’t know I was a dragon, not yet, who saw me only for me.”<br /><br />“She was impulsive, reckless, infuriating…and I couldn’t imagine my life without her.”<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Harlequin Teen provided me with a copy of Rogue. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9867345281088731213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1249123932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249123932" />
    <a title="Tilly Booth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23638789-tilly-booth"><img alt="Tilly Booth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530277607p2/23638789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249123932?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tilly Booth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tilly Booth" href="/user/show/23638789-tilly-booth">Tilly Booth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249123932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16776793599450156110">Rogue, the second book in the Talon series was a let down for me. When I finished Talon I was really hoping that the second book would be even better. I was hoping for more badass dragons, more drama, and just more in general but if anything, it lacked all of those things. <br/><br/>Rogue was predictable. I knew what was going to happen at the end of this book as soon as I begun it. The characters predictable. I don't feel like there's any huge love connections in this book even though Ember has two guys </span>
  <span id="freeText16776793599450156110" style="display:none">Rogue, the second book in the Talon series was a let down for me. When I finished Talon I was really hoping that the second book would be even better. I was hoping for more badass dragons, more drama, and just more in general but if anything, it lacked all of those things. <br /><br />Rogue was predictable. I knew what was going to happen at the end of this book as soon as I begun it. The characters predictable. I don't feel like there's any huge love connections in this book even though Ember has two guys that are both in love with her. I just don't see a huge amount of chemistry between them all. In saying that though, I do like that she has two sides. Her human side, attracted to the human boy and her dragon side, that wants the dragon boy. But it's been two books of her shuffling her feet between them when there's bigger things happening. <br /><br />I think the best part about this book is the epilogue. I find that in Talon and Rogue that the short snippets at the end are what make me pick up the next book. It's probably the only part of this story that piques my interest. For that alone, I will consider picking up the next book when it's released but until then...I'll be imagining all the other great ways this book could've gone. The story line has so much potential. Sadly, it's gone to waste. For that, I give Rogue by Julie Kagawa 1 out 5. <br /><br />I received this ebook from the publishers through NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16776793599450156110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15724491939632588242">★★★½<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23168406.Rogue__Talon__2_' title='Rogue (Talon #2) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rogue</a> is the second installment in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa' title='Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julie Kagawa</a>'s young adult, fantasy trilogy titled: <u>Talon</u>. I had a bit of difficulty getting into this middle book, and for a while I was fearful this would be your classic "filler book", but I am happy to say it got better! Lots of action, plot twists, young-adult romance (and yes, unfortunately more of the dreaded love triangle). I'm pretty confident fans of this trilogy will be happy. If you like fantasy/paranormal-themed stories about dragon shifters an</span>
  <span id="freeText15724491939632588242" style="display:none">★★★½<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23168406.Rogue__Talon__2_" title="Rogue (Talon #2) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Rogue</a> is the second installment in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a>'s young adult, fantasy trilogy titled: <u>Talon</u>. I had a bit of difficulty getting into this middle book, and for a while I was fearful this would be your classic "filler book", but I am happy to say it got better! Lots of action, plot twists, young-adult romance (and yes, unfortunately more of the dreaded love triangle). I'm pretty confident fans of this trilogy will be happy. If you like fantasy/paranormal-themed stories about dragon shifters and have historically enjoyed trilogies such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17929102.Legend_Trilogy_Boxed_Set__Legend___1_3_" title="Legend Trilogy Boxed Set (Legend, #1-3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> then the <u>Talon</u> trilogy is for you!<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“You burn so hot, and so bright, you set everything around you on fire. Just be careful that the people around you don’t get singed,” he said in a low voice. “Or that you don’t burn too hot, too quickly. The brightest flames are usually the ones that are extinguished first.”</i></span>

    <a title="Sandra (LadyGrey Reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25293586-sandra-ladygrey-reads"><img alt="Sandra (LadyGrey Reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517138745p2/25293586.jpg" /></a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25293586-sandra-ladygrey-reads?shelf=series-that-i-have-finished">series-that-i-have-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25293586-sandra-ladygrey-reads?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358047355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13926589525216389433"><blockquote>
  <b>The hardest thing about waiting to die is being torn between wanting more time and wishing they would just get it over with already.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524996880ra/25451910.gif' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Basically me during this book. It definitely suffered a bit from "second book syndrome".<br/><br/>It was a good sequel, in a way, but it did not feel like the story or the characters progressed much. It just felt like a lot of waiting for the next book. I did not like how naive Ember appeared, how much she seemed inclined to run from everything, how much she led both Rile</span>
  <span id="freeText13926589525216389433" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>The hardest thing about waiting to die is being torn between wanting more time and wishing they would just get it over with already.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524996880ra/25451910.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Basically me during this book. It definitely suffered a bit from "second book syndrome".<br><br>It was a good sequel, in a way, but it did not feel like the story or the characters progressed much. It just felt like a lot of waiting for the next book. I did not like how naive Ember appeared, how much she seemed inclined to run from everything, how much she led both Riley and Garrett on - although I did start to form a theory as to why this last thing was happening towards the end of the book, which did make it a bit more bearable and also a bit inspiring for one of my own stories, so I'm not complaining that much about this situation.<br><br>I did, however, like the fact that we got more chapters from Dante's POV. I liked finding out more about what it was like inside of Talon - because, hell, brainwashing much? And when things started to indicate that also St George might be corrupted, it got a bit more interesting. So I will give this particular book the benefit of the doubt and believe that the story will get more exciting in the following novels.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LYRCG96dTK7zJvaLGSA58QRm51tu216KjSHh3B9qSsleffsa+LalbqOqYmXL9WE1tg7FnkhYDNKxoGg8WuVlVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q16ffOJZPYP1eIyrdiYIBzbBoWW/HushRpnI2b5LzqvYpyZ9xHLUQ6X0GEWk81DDhKmDoJmduXl6GEE5+8ThNw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
